				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce.com&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Salesforce.com">Salesforce.com</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<p><b>Salesforce.com, Inc.</b> is an American cloud-based software company headquartered in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco, California</a>. It provides <a href="/wiki/Customer-relationship_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Customer-relationship management">customer-relationship management</a> (CRM) service and also sells a complementary suite of enterprise applications focused on customer service, marketing automation, analytics, and application development.

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<p>The company was founded in 1999 by former <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a> executive <a href="/wiki/Marc_Benioff" title="Marc Benioff">Marc Benioff</a>, Parker Harris, Dave Moellenhoff, and Frank Dominguez as a <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">software as a service</a> (<a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">SaaS</a>) company.<sup id="cite_ref-Babcock_2009-12-29_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babcock_2009-12-29-4">[4]</a></sup> The team wrote the initial sales automation software, and launched it to customers between September and November 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2004, the company had its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> under the stock symbol CRM and raised US$110 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Compton_2004-06-23_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Compton_2004-06-23-6">[6]</a></sup> Early investors include <a href="/wiki/Larry_Ellison" title="Larry Ellison">Larry Ellison</a>, Magdalena Yesil, <a href="/wiki/Halsey_Minor" title="Halsey Minor">Halsey Minor</a>, Stewart Henderson, Mark Iscaro, and Igor Sill of Geneva Venture Partners.
</p><p>In July 2012, Salesforce applied to trademark to the term "<a href="/wiki/Social_enterprise" title="Social enterprise">social enterprise</a>" in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> where the term was in widespread use to describe businesses with a primarily social purpose. This was successfully challenged by a campaign called <i>#notinourname</i> which was launched by <a href="/wiki/Social_Enterprise_UK" title="Social Enterprise UK">Social Enterprise UK</a>, resulting in Salesforce.com withdrawing their trademark application and agreeing not to use the term in their future marketing.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2014, Salesforce announced the development of its Customer Success Platform to tie together Salesforce's services, including sales, service, marketing, analytics, community, and mobile apps.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In October 2017, Salesforce launched a <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> Analytics tool for <a href="/wiki/Business_marketing" title="Business marketing">business-to-business marketers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In September 2018, Salesforce partnered with <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> intended on improving apps for businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2020, co-chief operating office Keith Block stepped down from his position in the company. <a href="/wiki/Marc_Benioff" title="Marc Benioff">Marc Benioff</a> will remain as chairman and chief executive officer.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Services" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>Salesforce.com's <a href="/wiki/Customer-relationship_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Customer-relationship management">customer-relationship management</a> (CRM) service comprises several broad categories: Commerce Cloud, Sales Cloud,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Service Cloud,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Data Cloud<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> (including <a href="#Data-dot-com">Jigsaw</a>), <a href="/wiki/Salesforce_Marketing_Cloud" title="Salesforce Marketing Cloud">Marketing Cloud</a>, Community Cloud<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> (including Chatter), Analytics Cloud,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> App Cloud, and IoT with over 100,000 customers.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Active">Active</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Active" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Salesforce">Salesforce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Salesforce" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Salesforce is the primary enterprise offering within the Salesforce platform. It provides companies with an interface for case management and task management, and a system for automatically routing and escalating important events. The Salesforce customer portal provides customers the ability to track their own cases, includes a social networking <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plug-in</a> that enables the user to join the conversation about their company on <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_service" title="Social networking service">social networking Web sites</a>, provides analytical tools and other services including email alert, Google search, and access to customers' entitlement and contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Lightning_Platform">Lightning Platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Lightning Platform" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Lightning Platform<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> (also known as Force.com) is a <a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_service" title="Platform as a service">platform as a service</a> (PaaS) that allows developers to create add-on applications that integrate into the main Salesforce.com application.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2017)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> These third-party applications are hosted on Salesforce.com's infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p><p>Force.com applications are built using declarative tools, backed by Lightning<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (November 2017)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and Apex, a proprietary <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>-like programming language for Force.com, <sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> as well as Lightning and Visualforce, a framework<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> including an XML<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> syntax typically used to generate <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>). The Force.com platform typically receives three complete releases a year.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> As the platform is provided as a service to its developers, every single development instance also receives all these updates.
</p><p>In the Spring 2015 release a new framework for building user interfaces – Lightning Components – was introduced in beta.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Lightning components are built using the open-source Aura Framework<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> but with support for Apex as the server-side language instead of Aura's <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">Javascript</a> dependency. This has been described as an alternative to, not necessarily a replacement for, Visualforce pages.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>According to a September 2009 <a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner Group</a> report,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Force.com had over 1,000 customer accounts. As of 2013, the Force.com platform has 1.4 million registered developers.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p><p>Lightning Base Components is the component library built on top of Lightning Web Components.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_Cloud">Community Cloud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Community Cloud" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Community Cloud provides Salesforce customers the ability to create online web properties for external collaboration, customer service, channel sales, and other custom portals in their instance of Salesforce. Tightly integrated to Sales Cloud, Service Cloud, and App Cloud, Community Cloud can be quickly customized to provide a wide variety of web properties. Community Cloud combines the functionality of the former Salesforce Customer and Partner Portals with some additional features.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Work.com">Work.com</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Work.com" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Work.com, previously <b>Rypple</b>, is a social performance management platform that helps managers and employees improve work performance through continuous coaching, real-time feedback, and recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> It is marketed as a solution for <a href="/wiki/Sales_management" title="Sales management">sales performance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Customer_service" title="Customer service">customer service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marketing" title="Marketing">marketing</a>, and as a service that can be employed by <a href="/wiki/Human_resource_management" title="Human resource management">human resource departments</a>.
</p><p>Work.com, then known as "Rypple", was founded by Daniel Debow and David Stein, who wanted to create a simple way of asking for feedback anonymously at work.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The company was formed in May 2008 and their client list included <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/LinkedIn" title="LinkedIn">LinkedIn</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gilt_Groupe" title="Gilt Groupe">Gilt Groupe</a>. Rypple "'reverses the onus on the demand for more feedback' by getting employees to build and manage their own coaching networks".<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2011, Rypple announced that they had hired Bohdan Zabawskyj as its Chief Technology Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, Rypple developed a more formalized management methodology called <a href="/wiki/OKR" title="OKR">OKR</a> ("Objectives and Key Results") for <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Rypple also partnered with Facebook to create "Loops", short for "feedback loops", which gathers feedback from co-workers, "thank you's", progress against goals, and coaching from supervisors into one channel for a "rich, robust, continuous performance review".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2011, Salesforce.com announced that they would acquire Rypple. The transaction was completed in 2012 and Rypple was rebranded as Work.com in September 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="AppExchange">AppExchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: AppExchange" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Launched in 2005, the Salesforce AppExchange is an online <a href="/wiki/App_store" title="App store">application marketplace</a> for third-party applications that run on the Force.com platform. Applications are available for free, as well as via yearly or monthly subscription models. Applications available range from integrations with <a href="/wiki/SharePoint" title="SharePoint">SharePoint</a> to mobile approval management.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> As of June 2016, it features 2,948 applications which have driven 3+ million installs.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The "AppExchange" is also a place customers can search for cloud consulting partners to help them implement the technology in their own organization. Cloud consulting partners for Salesforce include large companies like <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s "Bluewolf" and <a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a> as well as smaller ones like <a href="/wiki/Cloudreach" title="Cloudreach">Cloudreach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="myTrailhead">myTrailhead</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: myTrailhead" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Announced in 2017 and launched in 2019, Salesforce's myTrailhead is an online training platform that can be customized for the specific needs of its customers. The platform extends functionality which Salesforce built to provide users with training content specific to their usage of Salesforce and enables users to create and publish their own training content and programs.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Blockchain_platform">Blockchain platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Blockchain platform" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Announced on May 29, 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Salesforce launched a blockchain platform<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> based on <a href="/wiki/Hyperledger#Hyperledger_Sawtooth" title="Hyperledger">Hyperledger Sawtooth</a> to facilitate building blockchain network and apps integrated with CRM.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>Salesforce, announced in April 2019 a blockchain offering on top of Hyperledger Sawtooth<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_or_end-of-life">Retired or end-of-life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Retired or end-of-life" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Data.com"><span id="Data-dot-com"></span>Data.com</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Data.com" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Data.com, previously known as Jigsaw, was a cloud-based automated system for acquiring and managing CRM records within a user's Salesforce.com account.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>Data.com was also an online business directory of companies and business professionals that is built, maintained and accessed by a worldwide community of over a million subscribers.,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The information consisted of what is commonly found on a <a href="/wiki/Business_card" title="Business card">business card</a>.
</p><p>Data.com competitors included services such as <a href="/wiki/Dun_%26_Bradstreet" title="Dun &amp; Bradstreet">Dun &amp; Bradstreet</a>/Avention and <a href="/wiki/ZoomInfo" title="ZoomInfo">ZoomInfo</a>.
</p><p>Data.com was made up of three products: Data.com Connect, Data.com Clean and Data.com Prospector.
</p><p>In April 2018, Salesforce announced it would retire Data.com Connect on May 4, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p><p>Salesforce also announced it will wind down Data.com Clean and Data.com Prospector, and these services will close on July 31, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Desk.com">Desk.com</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Desk.com" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Desk.com is a <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">saas</a> <a href="/wiki/Help_desk" title="Help desk">help desk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Customer_support" title="Customer support">customer support</a> product accessible through the cloud. Desk.com is owned by Salesforce.com and was previously known as Assistly. Desk.com is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco, California</a>.
</p><p>After being acquired by Salesforce.com for $50 million in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-Techcrunch_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Techcrunch-56">[56]</a></sup> Assistly was re-branded as Desk.com in 2012<sup id="cite_ref-Desk.com_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Desk.com-57">[57]</a></sup> as a <a href="/wiki/Customer_support" title="Customer support">customer support</a> <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Venturebeat_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venturebeat-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>Desk.com is a Saas customer service application. The product differentiates itself from Salesforce's other service platform in that Desk.com specifically targets small businesses with its features and functions.<sup id="cite_ref-PC_World_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PC_World-59">[59]</a></sup> Desk.com integrates with a variety of products and third-party applications including Salesforce CRM, Salesforce IQ,<sup id="cite_ref-Salesforce_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salesforce-60">[60]</a></sup> Atlassian JIRA, Mailchimp<sup id="cite_ref-Mailchimp_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mailchimp-61">[61]</a></sup> and other apps. Desk.com also supports up to 50 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-Computerworld_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Computerworld-62">[62]</a></sup></p><p>Salesforce announced the retirement of desk.com, replacing it with Service Cloud Lightning. After March 13, 2018 no new desk.com licenses were sold, and the retirement date was announced as March 13, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Do.com">Do.com</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Do.com" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Do.com was a cloud-based <a href="/wiki/Task_management" title="Task management">task management</a> system for small groups and businesses, introduced in 2011 and discontinued in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Salesforce did not offer any reason for shutting down the service, however, it provided an Export tool to save data entered within the Do.com interface. The Do.com domain was sold to a startup in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Configuration">Configuration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Configuration" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Salesforce users can configure their CRM application. In the system, there are tabs such as "Contacts," "Reports," and "Accounts." Each tab contains associated information. Configuration can be done on each tab by adding user-defined custom fields.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>Configuration can also be done at the "platform" level by adding configured applications to a Salesforce instance, that is adding sets of customized / novel tabs for specific vertical- or function-level (Finance, Human Resources, etc.) features.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Web_services">Web services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Web services" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In addition to the web interface, Salesforce offers a <a href="/wiki/SOAP" title="SOAP">SOAP</a>/<a href="/wiki/Representational_state_transfer" title="Representational state transfer">REST</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_service" title="Web service">Web service</a> <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">application programming interface</a> (API) that enables integration with other systems.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Technologies">Technologies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Technologies" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. </p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Apex">Apex</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Apex" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Apex is a proprietary programming language provided by the Force.com platform to developers similar to <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>. It is a strongly typed, object-oriented, case-insensitive programming language, following a dot-notation and curly-brackets syntax. Apex can be used to execute programmed functions during most processes on the Force.com platform including custom buttons and links, event handlers on record insertion, update, or deletion, via scheduling, or via the custom controllers of Visualforce pages.
</p><p>Due to the multitenant nature of the platform, the language has strictly imposed governor limitations<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> to guard against any code monopolizing shared resources. Salesforce provides a series of <a href="/wiki/Asynchrony_(computer_programming)" title="Asynchrony (computer programming)">asynchronous processing</a> methods for Apex to allow developers to produce longer-running and more complex Apex code.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Lightning">Lightning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Lightning" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, Salesforce made public the <a href="/wiki/Front_and_back_ends" class="mw-redirect" title="Front and back ends">front end</a> of its platform, called Lightning.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> This component-based framework is what the Salesforce mobile app is built on. Salesforce built on this framework in 2015 by releasing the Lightning Design System,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> an HTML style framework with default CSS styling built in. This framework allows customers to build their own components to either use in their internal instances or sell on the AppExchange.
</p><p>The Salesforce Lightning App Builder is a tool for <a href="/wiki/Rapid_application_development" title="Rapid application development">rapid application development</a> of responsive web interfaces. This interface allows for different screens to be put together based on Lightning components. This can be used as layouts for records or specific applications.
</p><p>Lightning Experience, released in 2016, is the new redesigned interface in Salesforce for processes enhancement. Since then all the apps available on AppExchange need to be Lightning and those built on Classic have to migrate to Lightning as Classic is not to be updated any more by Salesforce. The platform offers an option for developers to employ migration techniques to enable the new user interface and switch to Lightning.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SalesforceCustomerCompanyTour4.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/SalesforceCustomerCompanyTour4.JPG/220px-SalesforceCustomerCompanyTour4.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/SalesforceCustomerCompanyTour4.JPG/220px-SalesforceCustomerCompanyTour4.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SalesforceCustomerCompanyTour4.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A discussion panel at Salesforce's <i>Customer Company Tour</i> event that focused on customer relationship management</div></div></div>
<p>Salesforce is headquartered in San Francisco, with regional headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Morges" title="Morges">Morges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (covering Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, and Africa, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>), India (covering Asia Pacific minus Japan), and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> (covering Japan). Other major offices are in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo,_California" title="San Mateo, California">San Mateo, California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salesforce_Tower_(Indianapolis)" title="Salesforce Tower (Indianapolis)">Indianapolis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hillsboro,_Oregon" title="Hillsboro, Oregon">Hillsboro, Oregon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Salesforce.com has its services translated into 16<sup id="cite_ref-Read_Write_Web_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Read_Write_Web-76">[76]</a></sup> different languages and as of July 31, 2011, had 104,000<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> customers and over 2.1 million subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Salesforce moved its Midwest Regional headquarters to Indianapolis in 2017.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salesforce_Tower_New_York.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Salesforce_Tower_New_York.jpg/220px-Salesforce_Tower_New_York.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2291" data-file-height="2159"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 207px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Salesforce_Tower_New_York.jpg/220px-Salesforce_Tower_New_York.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="207" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salesforce_Tower_New_York.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Salesforce Tower in New York City.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a> included Salesforce, at the same time as <a href="/wiki/Fastenal" title="Fastenal">Fastenal</a>, into the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500_Index" title="S&amp;P 500 Index">S&amp;P 500 Index</a> in September 2008, following the <a href="/wiki/Federal_takeover_of_Fannie_Mae_and_Freddie_Mac" title="Federal takeover of Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac">federal takeover of Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac</a> and their removal from the index.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Leadership" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Marc_Benioff" title="Marc Benioff">Marc Benioff</a>, Chairman &amp; CEO, co-founder of the company (1999– )<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>Parker Harris, Co-Founder, oversees product strategy (1999– )<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>Bret Taylor, President, Chief Product Officer (2017– )<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li>Suzanne DiBianca, Executive Vice President, Corporate Relations and Chief Philanthropy Officer (2000– )<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Chief Communications Officer (2017– )<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li>Mark Hawkins, President and Chief Financial Officer (2014– )<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li>Elizabeth Pinkham, Executive Vice President, Global Real Estate (2000–)<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li>Tony Prophet, Chief Equality Officer (2016– )<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li>Stephanie Buscemi, Chief Marketing Officer (2018– )</li>
<li>Cindy Robbins, President and Chief People Officer (2006– )<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>Amy Weaver, President, Legal and General Counsel (2013– )<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Finances" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>For the fiscal year 2019, Salesforce reported revenue of US$3.28 billion, an increase of 26% year-over-year and 26% in constant currency. The CRM giant reported subscription and support revenues of US$12.41 billion, an increase of 27% year-over-year. Salesforce ranked 240 on the 2019 Fortune 500 list of the largest United States companies by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.salesforce.com/company/news-press/stories/2019/05/051619-k/">"Reaching New Heights on the Fortune 500 List| CRM"</a>. <i>www.salesforce.com</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. </td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="IT_infrastructure">IT infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: IT infrastructure" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Salesforce migrated to <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a> servers with <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Micro_Devices" title="Advanced Micro Devices">Advanced Micro Devices</a> processors running Linux from <a href="/wiki/Sun_Fire_15K#Sun_Fire_E25K" title="Sun Fire 15K">Sun Fire E25K</a> servers with SPARC processors running Solaris in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The company uses the Momentum platform from Message Systems to allow its customers to send large amounts of email.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, Salesforce announced plans to build a <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data center</a> in the UK to handle European citizens' personal data.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p><p>In 2013, Salesforce and Oracle announced a nine-year partnership in which Salesforce will use <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Linux" title="Oracle Linux">Oracle Linux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Exadata" title="Oracle Exadata">Oracle Exadata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Database" title="Oracle Database">Oracle Database</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Java_(software_platform)" title="Java (software platform)">Java platform</a> to power Salesforce's applications and SaaS platform.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>In 2016, Salesforce announced that it will use <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services" title="Amazon Web Services">Amazon Web Services</a> hosting for countries with restrictive data residency requirements and where no Salesforce data centers are operating. In July 2017, the first such Salesforce instance went live in Canada, with Salesforce announcing that this enabled signing a number of Canadian customers.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Acquisitions" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Criticisms" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<table class="box-Criticism_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-criticism" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article's <i>Criticism</i> or <i>Controversy</i> section <b>may compromise the article's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutral point of view</a> of the subject</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Article_structure" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">integrate the section's contents</a> into the article as a whole, or rewrite the material.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2017</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Subject_to_a_phishing_attack">Subject to a phishing attack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Subject to a phishing attack" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In November 2007 a successful <a href="/wiki/Phishing" title="Phishing">phishing</a> attack on a Salesforce employee compromised contact information on a number of Salesforce customers, which was then used to send highly targeted phishing emails.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Salesforce has stated that "a phisher tricked someone into disclosing a password, but this intrusion did not stem from a security flaw in [the salesforce.com] application or database."<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The phishing breach was cited as an example of why the CRM industry needs greater security for users against such threats as <a href="/wiki/Spamming" title="Spamming">spam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p><p>While the crowd-sourced method of building business contacts<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> has proven popular with recruiters, marketers, and sales professionals, it has also raised questions of privacy as most of the site's database is entered without permission from the person being listed. Data.com does, however, make it easy to remove business information on request as noted in December 2009 by <a href="/wiki/TechCrunch" title="TechCrunch">TechCrunch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> However, recipients of these messages regard it as spam and at least one complaint about receiving more spam after attempting to remove one's address has been noted.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id=".E2.80.98Meatpistol.E2.80.99_presenters_let_go_at_Def_Con"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="‘Meatpistol’_presenters_let_go_at_Def_Con">‘Meatpistol’ presenters let go at Def Con</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: ‘Meatpistol’ presenters let go at Def Con" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2017 at <a href="/wiki/DEF_CON" title="DEF CON">Def Con</a>, Salesforce's Director of Offensive Security and a security engineer were fired on the conference room floor in front of several other attendees by an executive at the company after giving a talk. Word rapidly spread that two speakers had been released at the event.<sup id="cite_ref-Ars2017DefCon_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ars2017DefCon-158">[158]</a></sup> The presentation was initially signed off on by the company; however, Salesforce's management team had an unexplained and sudden change of heart an hour before the event.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Salesforce's Director of Offensive Security had turned off his phone prior to the presentation and was unable to receive any communication from Salesforce prior to the presentation.<sup id="cite_ref-Ars2017DefCon_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ars2017DefCon-158">[158]</a></sup> Reaction after the firings were swift, with the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a> providing representation to the fired employees<sup id="cite_ref-Ars2017DefCon_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ars2017DefCon-158">[158]</a></sup> and members of the security community opining "Salesforce undermined their credibility in the security community to a significant degree" and that "how they are perceived by the security community isn't top of their list of things they care about."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> The presented MEATPISTOL tool was anticipated to be released as open-source at the time of the presentation, but Salesforce continues to hold back on releasing any of the code to developers or the public.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The terminated employees have continued to call on the company to open-source the software.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="RAICES_donation_refusal">RAICES donation refusal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: RAICES donation refusal" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">not-for-profit</a> organization <a href="/wiki/Refugee_and_Immigrant_Center_for_Education_and_Legal_Services" title="Refugee and Immigrant Center for Education and Legal Services">Refugee and Immigrant Center for Education and Legal Services</a> (RAICES) rejected a US$250,000 philanthropic donation from Salesforce because the company has contracts with <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">Customs and Border Patrol</a> [sic]. The executive director of Raices, Jonathan Ryan, tweeted that "When it comes to supporting oppressive, inhumane, and illegal policies, we want to be clear: the only right action is to stop" in reference to the rejected donation.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Salesforce CEO <a href="/wiki/Marc_Benioff" title="Marc Benioff">Marc Benioff</a> responded in an <a href="/wiki/Press_release" title="Press release">official statement</a> that the company's employees "don't work with <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">CBP</a> regarding separation of families. CBP is a customer &amp; follows our <a href="/wiki/Terms_of_service" title="Terms of service">TOS</a>. We don't have an agreement with <a href="/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement" title="U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement">ICE</a>. I'm Proud of the Men &amp; Women who protect &amp; serve our country every day &amp; I'm Proud of our <a href="/wiki/Ohana" title="Ohana">Ohana</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p><p>It was reported that, in a change to its acceptable-use policy,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Salesforce is barring customers from using its system to sell semiautomatic guns and other firearms.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_avoidance">Tax avoidance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tax avoidance" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In December 2019, <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> listed Salesforce.com along with 378 additional <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500"><i>Fortune</i> 500</a> companies that "paid an effective federal tax rate of 0% or less" as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Tax_Cuts_and_Jobs_Act_of_2017" title="Tax Cuts and Jobs Act of 2017">Tax Cuts and Jobs Act of 2017</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuit">Lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Lawsuit" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>In March 2019 Salesforce faced a lawsuit by 50 anonymous women claiming to be victims and survivors of <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking_in_the_United_States" title="Sex trafficking in the United States">sex trafficking</a>, abuse and rape, which alleges the company profited from and knowingly facilitated sex trafficking on the Web site <a href="/wiki/Backpage" title="Backpage">Backpage</a>.com (defunct since April 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune-169">[169]</a></sup> The lawsuit also pointed out that ironically Salesforce was publicly promoting an anti-<a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a> campaign at the time of its work with Backpage.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawsuit_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawsuit-170">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Barron's_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barron's-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Salesforce_Venture_Capital">Salesforce Venture Capital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Salesforce Venture Capital" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>In 2009, in response to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">financial crisis of 2007–2008</a> and the resulting decline in venture funding, Salesforce began investing in digital companies that used or integrated Salesforce platform.<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson,_BI_8/18/2018_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson,_BI_8/18/2018-172">[172]</a></sup> This eventually became Salesforce Ventures, headed by John Somorjai<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson,_BI_8/18/2018_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson,_BI_8/18/2018-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Since then various funds have been created to focus on specific areas — in September 2014 SFV set up Salesforce1 Fund, aimed at start-ups creating applications primarily for mobile phones. In December 2018, Salesforce Ventures announced the launch of the Japan Trailblazer Fund, focused on Japanese startups.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p><p>As of August 2018, Salesforce Ventures reported investments totaling $1.2 billion in 275 companies covering a wide range of business models, including e-commerce (CloudCraze),<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Figure_Eight_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Figure Eight (company) (page does not exist)">Figure Eight</a>), online fraud prevention (<a href="/wiki/Forter" title="Forter">Forter</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Accounting and Professional Services Automation software (FinancialForce)<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> and many other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Its five largest investments <a href="/wiki/Domo_(company)" title="Domo (company)">Domo</a> (data-visualization software), <a href="/wiki/SurveyMonkey" title="SurveyMonkey">SurveyMonkey</a> (online survey software), <a href="/wiki/Twilio" title="Twilio">Twilio</a> (cloud-communication), <a href="/wiki/Dropbox_(service)" title="Dropbox (service)">Dropbox</a> (cloud storage), and <a href="/wiki/DocuSign" title="DocuSign">DocuSign</a> (secure e-signature company) account for nearly half of its portfolio.<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_BI_11/14/2018_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson_BI_11/14/2018-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Salesforce&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
